2025-08-06 16:31:39.170 | INFO     | metagpt.actions.write_prd:run:86 - New requirement detected: Create a ticket management web application that allows users to report issues at a university campus (facility management problems, technical IT issues and services complaints). The application allows users to report and modify problems, and interacts with helpdesk staff who is taking care of the issue.

The application uses a database to store all the data and enables the helpdesk staff to visualize the data and select the analysis to perform.

Use python programming language.
# Requirements:

## Login page:
    - Generate a GUI that allows users to enter the application either as an helpdesk staff or a simple user.
    - Do not implement any login and user management system.

## Ticket management system:
    - Generate a GUI that enables following ticket management:
        - Simple user can insert a new ticket and view and modify all the 'open' and 'active' tickets.
        - Helpdesk users can view all the open, active and closed tickets. They can change ticket status from 'open' to 'active' and from 'active' to 'closed'.
        - Under each ticket, helpdesk users and simple users can exchange messages related to that ticket.
    - Ticket attributes:
        - Each ticket has a status assigned:
            - A newly created ticket has the status 'open' assigned by default.
            - Helpdesk users can change tickets status from 'open' to 'active' and from 'active' to 'closed'.
        - Each ticket has a free text description field.
        - Each ticket has an automatically assigned category among the following categories: facility management (e.g.: elevator is not working), technical IT (e.g.: WIFI malfunctioning), services complaints (e.g.: canteen's food complaints)
        - Each ticket has an opening, last modification and closing date attribute.
    - Database:
        - Implement a database to store tickets and users interaction data.
        - Implement all the basic functionalities that a database needs as inserting and modifying data.

## Micro-services architecture:
    - Implement a microservices architecture that interacts with the ticket management application to provide helpdesk users data visualization and analysis functionalities.
    - Interaction with the database should be enabled via API.
    - Implement the following services:
        - Service 1: Allow user to choose the period (last X hours/days). Display the number of tickets opened in the selected period, which have not yet been closed.
        - Service 2: Average ticket resolution time, displayed by the opening month (of the ticket)
        - Service 3: Cluster the tickets by ticket category and display number of active tickets per category.

Analytics microservices communicate via RESTful APIs.","Anything UNCLEAR":"Clarification on the specific GUI framework to be used is needed for more detailed UI design."}\n\n## Code Files\n----- models.py\n```## models.py\n\nfrom sqlalchemy import Column, Integer, String, DateTime, ForeignKey\nfrom sqlalchemy.orm import relationship\nfrom sqlalchemy.ext.declarative import declarative_base\nfrom datetime import datetime\n\nBase = declarative_base()\n\nclass TicketModel(Base):\n    __tablename__ = \'tickets\'\n    \n    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)\n    title = Column(String(256), nullable=False)\n    description = Column(String(1024), nullable=False)\n    status = Column(String(32), default=\'open\')\n    created_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)\n    updated_at = Column(DateTime, onupdate=datetime.utcnow)\n    comments = relationship("Comment", back_populates="ticket")\n\n    def __init__(self, title: str, description: str):\n        self.title = title\n        self.description = description\n\nclass Comment(Base):\n    __tablename__ = \'comments\'\n    \n    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)\n    ticket_id = Column(Integer, ForeignKey(\'tickets.id\'))\n    content = Column(String(1024), nullable=False)\n    created_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)\n\n    ticket = relationship("TicketModel", back_populates="comments")\n\n    def __init__(self, content: str):\n        self.content = content\n```\n\n\n## Code to be Reviewed: app.py\n```Code\n## app.py\nfrom flask import Flask, request, jsonify\nfrom models import TicketModel, Comment, Base\nfrom sqlalchemy import create_engine\nfrom sqlalchemy.orm import sessionmaker\nfrom .analytics_service import AnalyticsService  # Corrected import statement\n\napp = Flask(__name__)\n\n# Database setup\nDATABASE_URI = \'sqlite:///tickets.db\'\nengine = create_engine(DATABASE_URI)\nBase.metadata.create_all(engine)\nSession = sessionmaker(bind=engine)\n\n@app.route(\'/ticket\', methods=[\'POST\'])\ndef create_ticket():\n    data = request.get_json()\n    title = data[\'title\']\n    description = data[\'description\']\n\n    with Session() as session:\n        new_ticket = TicketModel(title=title, description=description)\n        session.add(new_ticket)\n        session.commit()\n\n    return jsonify({\'ticket_id\': new_ticket.id}), 201\n\n@app.route(\'/comment\', methods=[\'POST\'])\ndef add_comment():\n    data = request.get_json()\n    ticket_id = data[\'ticket_id\']\n    content = data[\'content\']\n\n    with Session() as session:\n        comment = Comment(content=content)\n        ticket = session.query(TicketModel).filter_by(id=ticket_id).first()\n\n        if not ticket:\n            return jsonify({\'error\': \'Ticket not found\'}), 404\n\n        ticket.comments.append(comment)\n        session.add(ticket)\n        session.commit()\n\n    return jsonify({\'comment_id\': comment.id}), 201\n\n@app.route(\'/analytics/resolution_times\', methods=[\'GET\'])\ndef get_resolution_times():\n    service = AnalyticsService()\n    resolution_times = service.get_resolution_times()\n    return jsonify(resolution_times), 200\n\n@app.route(\'/analytics/active_tickets_by_category\', methods=[\'GET\'])\ndef get_active_tickets_by_category():\n    service = AnalyticsService()\n    active_tickets = service.get_active_tickets_by_category()\n    return jsonify(active_tickets), 200\n\nif __name__ == \'__main__\':\n    app.run(debug=True)\n\n```\n\n\n\n# Format example 1\n## Code Review: app.py\n1. Column(String(256), nullable=False)\n    description = Column(String(1024), nullable=False)\n    status = Column(String(32), default=\'open\')\n    created_at = Column(DateTime, except Exception as e:\n            session.rollback()\n            return jsonify({\'error\': str(e)}), 500\n\n@app.route(\'/analytics/resolution_times\', methods=[\'GET\'])\ndef Initialize the database engine and session\n        DATABASE_URI = \'sqlite:///tickets.db\'\n        self.engine = create_engine(DATABASE_URI)\n        Session = sessionmaker(bind=self.engine)\n        self.session = Session()\n\n    def get_resolution_times(self) -> list[dict]:\n        """\n        Fetches resolution times for tickets.\n        \n        Returns:\n            A list of         A list of dictionaries containing ticket ID and its status.\n        """\n        # For demonstration, we assume a simple query to fetch data\n        # In real scenarios, this would involve analytics_service.py\nfrom sqlalchemy.orm import sessionmaker\nfrom models import TicketModel, Base\nfrom sqlalchemy import create_engine\n\nclass AnalyticsService:\n    def __init__(self):\n        # Initialize the database engine and session\n        DATABASE_URI = \'sqlite:///tickets.db\'\n        self.engine = create_engine(DATABASE_URI)\n        Session = sessionmaker(bind=self.engine)\n        self.session = Session()\n\n    def get_resolution_times(self) -> list[dict]:\n        """\n        Fetches resolution times for tickets.\n        \n        Returns:\n            A list of dictionaries containing ticket ID and its resolution time.\n        """\n        # For demonstration, we assume a simple query to fetch data\n        # In real scenarios, this would involve more complex logic\n        tickets = self.session.query(TicketModel).all()\n        result = [\n            {"ticket_id": t.id, "resolution_time": (t.updated_at - t.created_at).total_seconds() if t.status == \'closed\' else None}\n            for t in tickets\n        ]\n        return result\n\n    def get_active_tickets_by_category(self) -> list[dict]:\n        """\n        Fetches active tickets by category.\n        \n        Returns:\n            A list of dictionaries containing ticket ID and its status.\n        """\n        # For demonstration, we assume a simple query to fetch data\n        # In real scenarios, this would involve more complex logic\n        tickets = self.session.query(TicketModel).filter_by(status=\'open\').all()\n        result = [{"ticket_id": t.id, "category": self.session.close()\n\n```\n\n\n\n# Format example 1\n## Code Review: analytics_service.py\n1. 2025-08-06 16:43:54.912 | INFO     | metagpt.actions.write_prd:run:86 - New requirement detected: Create a ticket management web application that allows users to report issues at a university campus (facility management problems, technical IT issues and services complaints). The application allows users to report and modify problems, and interacts with helpdesk staff who is taking care of the issue.

The application uses a database to store all the data and enables the helpdesk staff to visualize the data and select the analysis to perform.

Use python programming language.
# Requirements:

## Login page:
    - Generate a GUI that allows users to enter the application either as an helpdesk staff or a simple user.
    - Do not implement any login and user management system.

## Ticket management system:
    - Generate a GUI that enables following ticket management:
        - Simple user can insert a new ticket and view and modify all the 'open' and 'active' tickets.
        - Helpdesk users can view all the open, active and closed tickets. They can change ticket status from 'open' to 'active' and from 'active' to 'closed'.
        - Under each ticket, helpdesk users and simple users can exchange messages related to that ticket.
    - Ticket attributes:
        - Each ticket has a status assigned:
            - A newly created ticket has the status 'open' assigned by default.
            - Helpdesk users can change tickets status from 'open' to 'active' and from 'active' to 'closed'.
        - Each ticket has a free text description field.
        - Each ticket has an automatically assigned category among the following categories: facility management (e.g.: elevator is not working), technical IT (e.g.: WIFI malfunctioning), services complaints (e.g.: canteen's food complaints)
        - Each ticket has an opening, last modification and closing date attribute.
    - Database:
        - Implement a database to store tickets and users interaction data.
        - Implement all the basic functionalities that a database needs as inserting and modifying data.

## Micro-services architecture:
    - Implement a microservices architecture that interacts with the ticket management application to provide helpdesk users data visualization and analysis functionalities.
    - Interaction with the database should be enabled via API.
    - Implement the following services:
        - Service 1: Allow user to choose the period (last X hours/days). Display the number of tickets opened in the selected period, which have not yet been closed.
        - Service 2: Average ticket resolution time, displayed by the opening month (of the ticket)
        - Service 3: Cluster the tickets by ticket category and display number of active tickets per category.

models.py\n```Code\nfrom sqlalchemy import Column, Integer, String, ForeignKey\nfrom sqlalchemy.ext.declarative import declarative_base\nfrom sqlalchemy.orm import relationship\n\nBase = declarative_base()\n\nclass User(Base):\n    """\n    Represents a user in the system.\n    \n    Attributes:\n        id (int): Unique identifier for the user.\n        username (str): Username chosen by the user.\n        email (str): Email address of the user.\n    """\n    __tablename__ = \'users\'\n    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)\n    username = Column(String, nullable=False)\n    email = Column(String, nullable=False)\n\n    tickets = relationship(\'Ticket\', backref=\'user\')\n\n    def __init__(self, username: str, email: str):\n        """\n        Initializes a new User instance.\n        \n        Args:\n            username (str): Username chosen by the user.\n            email (str): Email address of the user.\n        """\n        self.username = username\n        self.email = email\n\n    def get_tickets(self) -> list:\n        """\n        Retrieves all tickets associated with this user.\n        \n        Returns:\n            list: List of Ticket instances.\n        """\n        return self.tickets\n\n\nclass Ticket(Base):\n    """\n    Represents a ticket in the system.\n    \n    Attributes:\n        id (int): Unique identifier for the ticket.\n        title (str): Title of the ticket.\n        description (str): Description of the ticket.\n        status (str): Status of the ticket.\n        user_id (int): Foreign key referencing the User who created this ticket.\n    """\n    __tablename__ = \'tickets\'\n    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)\n    title = Column(String, nullable=False)\n    description = Column(String, nullable=False)\n    status = Column(String, default=\'open\')\n    user_id = Column(Integer, ForeignKey(\'users.id\'))\n\n    messages = relationship(\'Message\', backref=\'ticket\')\n\n    def __init__(self, title: str, description: str, user_id: int):\n        """\n        Initializes a new Ticket instance.\n        \n        Args:\n            title (str): Title of the ticket.\n            description (str): Description of the ticket.\n            user_id (int): Foreign key referencing the User who created this ticket.\n        """\n        self.title = title\n        self.description = description\n        self.user_id = user_id\n\n    def update_status(self, status: str):\n        """\n        Updates the status of this ticket.\n        \n        Args:\n            status (str): New status for the ticket.\n        """\n        self.status = status\n\n    def get_messages(self) -> list:\n        """\n        Retrieves all messages associated
